\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{matplotlib-othercharts_files/figure-pdf/cell-3-output-1.pdf}}

\section{Box plot}\label{box-plot}

A box plot is used to present information about the distribution of
numeric data and to identify outliers. It is particularly useful when
analyzing continuous data that have different values and distributions.
Here are a few types of data for which a box plot can be used:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  Comparing groups: A box plot is used to compare the distribution of
  data between different groups. For example, it can be used to compare
  the test results of students from different schools, salaries in
  different sectors, or the sales values of different products.
\item
  Identifying outliers: A box plot is used to identify outliers in the
  data, which may indicate measurement errors, unusual observations, or
  extreme values. For example, it can be used to detect anomalies in
  meteorological data, stock market values, or medical data.
\item
  Distribution analysis: A box plot helps to understand the distribution
  of data, such as the median, quartiles, range of values, and potential
  outliers. It can be used in the analysis of data such as grades,
  population growth, stock value, or real estate prices.
\item
  Visualization of multidimensional data: A box plot can be used to
  visualize multidimensional data, presenting the distribution of many
  variables on a single chart. For example, you can compare variables
  such as age, earnings, and education in a demographic study.
\end{enumerate}

It is worth noting that a box plot is particularly useful when we want
to understand the distribution of data, but it does not show the
specific number of observations or the values of individual data points.
In such cases, other types of charts, such as a scatter plot, may be
more appropriate.

A box plot shows five descriptive statistics of the data: the minimum,
the first quartile (Q1), the median, the third quartile (Q3), and the
maximum.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ numpy }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ np}

\CommentTok{\# Example data}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.random.rand(}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Creating the chart}
\NormalTok{fig, ax }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.subplots()}

\CommentTok{\# Drawing the boxplot}
\NormalTok{ax.boxplot(data)}

\CommentTok{\# Adding labels}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Boxplot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Values\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_xticklabels([}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Example data\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{])}

\CommentTok{\# Displaying the chart}
\NormalTok{plt.show(block}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{matplotlib-othercharts_files/figure-pdf/cell-4-output-1.pdf}}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{m10.png}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ numpy }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ np}

\CommentTok{\# Creating dataset}
\NormalTok{np.random.seed(}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.random.normal(}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{20}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{200}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Creating plot}
\NormalTok{plt.boxplot(data)}

\CommentTok{\# show plot}
\NormalTok{plt.show(block}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{matplotlib-othercharts_files/figure-pdf/cell-5-output-1.pdf}}

\textbf{\texttt{patch\_artist=True,\ \ \ \ \#\ colored\ boxes}} --
enables the use of ``Patch'' objects to draw the boxes themselves, so
that we can fill them with color (further controlled by
\texttt{boxprops}).

\textbf{\texttt{notch=True,\ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \ \#\ notches\ at\ the\ median}}
-- draws a notch around the median line, which helps to visually assess
the significance of differences between medians.

\textbf{\texttt{boxprops=dict(facecolor=\textquotesingle{}lightblue\textquotesingle{},\ edgecolor=\textquotesingle{}navy\textquotesingle{}),}}
-- styling of the boxes themselves:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{facecolor=\textquotesingle{}lightblue\textquotesingle{}} --
  fills the box with a light blue color,
\item
  \texttt{edgecolor=\textquotesingle{}navy\textquotesingle{}} --
  outlines the box in dark navy.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{\texttt{medianprops=dict(color=\textquotesingle{}darkred\textquotesingle{}),}}
-- properties of the median line: only the dark red color
(\texttt{darkred}).

\textbf{\texttt{whiskerprops=dict(color=\textquotesingle{}navy\textquotesingle{}),}}
-- style of the whiskers: the ``navy'' color for the lines that connect
the box with the ends of the data range (without taking outliers into
account).

\textbf{\texttt{capprops=dict(color=\textquotesingle{}navy\textquotesingle{}),}}
-- style of the ``caps'' at the ends of the whiskers: also the navy
color.

\textbf{\texttt{flierprops=dict(}} -- style of the outlier points
(``fliers'', values beyond the reach of the whiskers):

\begin{verbatim}
* `marker='o'` – a circle as the marker,
* `markerfacecolor='gray'` – gray fill of the circle,
* `markersize=5` – the size of the marker,
* `linestyle='none'` – no line connecting these points.
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\CommentTok{\# Preparing the data}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(\{}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Mode of transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}
        \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Car\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Car\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Car\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Car\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Car\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
        \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Bicycle\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,    }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Bicycle\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,    }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Bicycle\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,    }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Bicycle\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,    }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Bicycle\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,}
        \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Public transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Public transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Public transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Public transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Public transport\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{    ],}

        \DecValTok{25}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{30}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{28}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{,}

        \DecValTok{40}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{45}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{42}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{38}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{44}
\NormalTok{    ]}
\NormalTok{\})}

\CommentTok{\# Preparing the data for the box plot}
\NormalTok{groups }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ data[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Mode of transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{].unique()}
\NormalTok{times\_list }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [data.loc[data[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Mode of transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{==}\NormalTok{ s, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Commute time (minutes)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
              \ControlFlowTok{for}\NormalTok{ s }\KeywordTok{in}\NormalTok{ groups]}

\CommentTok{\# Drawing the chart}
\NormalTok{plt.figure(figsize}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{8}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{6}\NormalTok{))}
\NormalTok{plt.boxplot(}
\NormalTok{    times\_list,}
\NormalTok{    tick\_labels}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{groups,}
\NormalTok{    patch\_artist}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,    }\CommentTok{\# colored boxes}
\NormalTok{    notch}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{,           }\CommentTok{\# notches at the median}
\NormalTok{    boxprops}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{dict}\NormalTok{(facecolor}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}lightblue\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, edgecolor}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}navy\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    medianprops}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{dict}\NormalTok{(color}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}darkred\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    whiskerprops}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{dict}\NormalTok{(color}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}navy\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    capprops}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{dict}\NormalTok{(color}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}navy\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{),}
\NormalTok{    flierprops}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{dict}\NormalTok{(marker}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}o\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, markerfacecolor}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}gray\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, markersize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{, linestyle}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}none\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Axis labels and title}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Commute time [minutes]\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Comparison of commute times to work}\CharTok{\textbackslash{}n}\StringTok{by mode of transport\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, fontsize}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{14}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Grid and aesthetics}
\NormalTok{plt.grid(axis}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}y\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, linestyle}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}{-}{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.7}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.tight\_layout()}

\CommentTok{\# Displaying}

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{matplotlib-othercharts_files/figure-pdf/cell-6-output-1.pdf}}

\section{Histogram}\label{histogram}

A histogram is used to present the distribution of numeric data, both
continuous and discrete. A histogram shows the frequency of occurrence
of data in specific intervals (bins), which allows for the analysis of
the distribution and the identification of patterns. Here are a few
types of data for which a histogram can be used:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  Distribution analysis: A histogram can be used to analyze the
  distribution of data, such as grades, prices, stock values, population
  growth, or meteorological data. This allows you to understand how the
  data is distributed, whether it is concentrated around certain values,
  or whether it has a long tail (i.e.~whether there are outliers).
\item
  Identifying trends: A histogram can help identify trends or patterns
  in data. For example, you can use a histogram to identify seasonal
  sales patterns, changes in stock market values, or population
  migration patterns.
\item
  Comparing groups: A histogram can also be used to compare the
  distribution of data between different groups. For example, it can be
  used to compare the test results of students from different schools,
  salaries in different sectors, or the sales values of different
  products.
\item
  Estimating parameters: A histogram can help estimate distribution
  parameters, such as the mean, median, or variance, which can be useful
  in statistical analysis.
\end{enumerate}

It is worth noting that a histogram is suitable for numeric data, but it
is not intended for presenting categorical data. In such cases, other
types of charts, such as a bar chart, may be more appropriate.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{x }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ [}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{7}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{8}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{9}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{,}

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{3D plots}\label{d-plots}

\subsection{Helix}\label{helix}

\[\begin{cases}
x=a\cos (t) \\
y=a\sin(t) \\
z=at
\end{cases}\]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ numpy }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ np}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{fig }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.figure()}
\NormalTok{ax }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.axes(projection}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}3d\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{t }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.linspace(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{15}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1000}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{a }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{3}
\NormalTok{xline }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ a }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.sin(t)}
\NormalTok{yline }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ a }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.cos(t)}
\NormalTok{zline }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ a }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ t}
\NormalTok{ax.plot3D(xline, yline, zline)}
\NormalTok{plt.show(block}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{matplotlib-othercharts_files/figure-pdf/cell-15-output-1.pdf}}

\subsection{Torus}\label{torus}

\[p(\alpha,\ \beta)=\Big((R+r\cos \alpha)\cos \beta,\ (R+r\cos \alpha)\sin \beta,\ r\sin \alpha\Big)\]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ numpy }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ np}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{fig }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.figure()}
\NormalTok{ax }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.axes(projection}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}3d\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{r }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{1}
\NormalTok{R }\OperatorTok{=} \DecValTok{5}
\NormalTok{alpha }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.arange(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2} \OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.pi, }\FloatTok{0.1}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{beta }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.arange(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2} \OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.pi, }\FloatTok{0.1}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{alpha, beta }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ np.meshgrid(alpha, beta)}
\NormalTok{x }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ (R }\OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ r }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.cos(alpha)) }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.cos(beta)}
\NormalTok{y }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ (R }\OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ r }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.cos(alpha)) }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.sin(beta)}
\NormalTok{z }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ r }\OperatorTok{*}\NormalTok{ np.sin(alpha)}
\NormalTok{ax.plot\_wireframe(x, y, z)}
\NormalTok{plt.show(block}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{matplotlib-othercharts_files/figure-pdf/cell-16-output-1.pdf}}

\chapter{Matplotlib - heatmap}\label{matplotlib---heatmap}

A heatmap is a two-dimensional visualization in which numeric values are
represented using colors. The intensity of the color corresponds to the
magnitude (value) at a specific point on the grid.

\textbf{Main applications of heatmaps}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Correlation matrices}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    They allow you to quickly identify strong and weak relationships
    between variables in a dataset.\\
  \item
    They facilitate the preliminary selection of features, e.g.~in
    predictive modeling.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Spatio-temporal analysis}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Visualization of the intensity of events (e.g.~sales, network
    traffic) along the time axis versus categories or zones.\\
  \item
    It helps to detect seasonal, daily, or weekly patterns.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Geographic maps}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Presentation of the density of events or values (e.g.~illnesses,
    accidents) across geographic areas.\\
  \item
    They enable the quick identification of ``hotspots''.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{User behavior analysis}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Tracking clicks, mouse movement, or scrolling on
    websites/applications.\\
  \item
    Optimization of the layout of interface elements for usability.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Resource and performance monitoring}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Visualization of server load, memory usage, or production output in
    real time.\\
  \item
    It helps to catch anomalies or overloads.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Detecting anomalies and deviations}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Identification of unusual readings, e.g.~in medical, financial, or
    network data.\\
  \item
    Quick indication of areas requiring further analysis.
  \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Monday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Tuesday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Wednesday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Thursday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Friday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Time of day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Morning\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{5} \OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Afternoon\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{5} \OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Evening\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Number of customers\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{50}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{60}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{65}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{,    }\CommentTok{\# Morning}
                            \DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{130}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{125}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{140}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Afternoon}
                            \DecValTok{90}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{95}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{110}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{]    }\CommentTok{\# Evening}
\NormalTok{\}}

\NormalTok{df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(data)}


\NormalTok{heatmap\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ df.pivot(index}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, columns}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Time of day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, values}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Number of customers\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{plt.imshow(heatmap\_data,}
\NormalTok{           cmap}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}YlOrRd\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,      }\CommentTok{\# palette from yellow (low) to red (high)}
\NormalTok{           aspect}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}auto\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)      }\CommentTok{\# automatic aspect ratio adjustment}

\NormalTok{cbar }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.colorbar()}
\NormalTok{cbar.set\_label(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Number of customers\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, rotation}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{270}\NormalTok{, labelpad}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{15}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{plt.xticks(ticks}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(}\BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(heatmap\_data.columns)),}
\NormalTok{           labels}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{heatmap\_data.columns,}
\NormalTok{           rotation}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{45}\NormalTok{,}
\NormalTok{           ha}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}right\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.yticks(ticks}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(}\BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(heatmap\_data.index)),}
\NormalTok{           labels}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{heatmap\_data.index)}

\NormalTok{plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Time of day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Day of the week\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Average number of customers in the store\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{plt.tight\_layout()}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Monday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Tuesday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Wednesday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Thursday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Friday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Time of day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Morning\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{5} \OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Afternoon\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{5} \OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Evening\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}\OperatorTok{*}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Number of customers\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{50}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{60}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{65}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{,    }\CommentTok{\# Morning}
                            \DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{130}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{125}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{140}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{,  }\CommentTok{\# Afternoon}
                            \DecValTok{90}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{95}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{110}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{]    }\CommentTok{\# Evening}
\NormalTok{\}}

\NormalTok{df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(data)}

\NormalTok{heatmap\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ df.pivot(index}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, columns}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Time of day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, values}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Number of customers\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{fig, ax }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ plt.subplots()}

\NormalTok{im }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ ax.imshow(}
\NormalTok{    heatmap\_data,}
\NormalTok{    cmap}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}YlOrRd\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,      }\CommentTok{\# palette from yellow (low) to red (high)}
\NormalTok{    aspect}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}auto\textquotesingle{}}       \CommentTok{\# automatic aspect ratio adjustment}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{cbar }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ fig.colorbar(im, ax}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ax)}
\NormalTok{cbar.set\_label(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Number of customers\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, rotation}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{270}\NormalTok{, labelpad}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{15}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{ax.set\_xticks(}\BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(}\BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(heatmap\_data.columns)))}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_xticklabels(heatmap\_data.columns, rotation}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{45}\NormalTok{, ha}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}right\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_yticks(}\BuiltInTok{range}\NormalTok{(}\BuiltInTok{len}\NormalTok{(heatmap\_data.index)))}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_yticklabels(heatmap\_data.index)}

\NormalTok{ax.set\_xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Time of day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Day of the week\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{ax.set\_title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Average number of customers in the store\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{fig.tight\_layout()}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\chapter{Matplotlib - area chart}\label{matplotlib---area-chart}

An area chart is a type of visualization in which successive data series
are presented as stacked areas/layers. The height of each layer
corresponds to the value of a given category, and the sum of the heights
of all layers shows the total value.

\section{Main applications of area
charts}\label{main-applications-of-area-charts}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Analysis of total composition over time}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    It allows you to see how individual components (e.g.~revenue
    sources, expenses, market segments) contribute to the total value at
    successive moments.\\
  \item
    Useful for monitoring percentage shares and changes in proportions.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Comparison of multidimensional trends}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    It enables the simultaneous tracking of many time series
    (``layers'') in a single space, which makes it easier to detect
    mutual correlations and turning points.\\
  \item
    Ideal for presenting multichannel data (e.g.~website traffic from
    different sources).
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Presentation of market shares or segments}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    It shows how the shares of individual products, regions, or customer
    groups change over time.\\
  \item
    It makes it easier to identify ``growing'' and ``shrinking''
    segments.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Budgeting and accounting}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    It visualizes the structure of costs or revenue by category over the
    course of the budget cycle.\\
  \item
    It helps to quickly catch excessive expenses or sources of revenue
    growth.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Monitoring resources and workloads}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Tracking the use of resources (e.g.~staff, machines) across
    different projects or departments.\\
  \item
    It enables planning and balancing the workload.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Comparison of scenarios or variants}

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Overlaying forecasted data alongside historical data makes it easier
    to compare the ``expected'' vs.~the ``actual'' behavior of
    indicators.\\
  \item
    It supports strategic decisions by illustrating deviations.
  \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Month\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}January\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}February\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}March\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}April\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}May\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{],}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Sales\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{1000}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1200}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{900}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1100}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1300}\NormalTok{],}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Services\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{200}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{250}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{230}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{260}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{300}\NormalTok{],}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Advertising\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{150}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{170}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{190}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{\}}

\NormalTok{df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(data)}

\NormalTok{x }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ df[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Month\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{y1 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ df[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Sales\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{y2 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ df[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Services\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{y3 }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ df[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Advertising\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}

\NormalTok{plt.figure(figsize}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{,}\DecValTok{6}\NormalTok{))}
\NormalTok{plt.stackplot(x, y1, y2, y3, labels}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Sales\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Services\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Advertising\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{plt.legend(loc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}upper left\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Company revenue broken down by source\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Month\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Amount (PLN)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xticks(rotation}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{45}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.tight\_layout()}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Day\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Monday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Tuesday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Wednesday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Thursday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Friday\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{],}

\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Number of visits\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.legend(loc}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}upper left\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.grid(axis}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}y\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, linestyle}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}{-}{-}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, alpha}\OperatorTok{=}\FloatTok{0.7}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xticks(rotation}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{45}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.tight\_layout()}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{matplotlib-areachart_files/figure-pdf/cell-4-output-1.pdf}}

\part{Seaborn}

\chapter{Seaborn - basics}\label{seaborn---basics}

\url{https://seaborn.pydata.org/}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

The Seaborn library, which is a wrapper around Matplotlib, makes it
easier to create ``beautiful and readable'' statistical charts in the
Python language.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  Exploratory data analysis (EDA): Seaborn is often used for data
  visualization during exploratory data analysis, which helps to
  understand the structure, trends, and relationships between variables
  in the data. This allows for the identification of patterns, the
  detection of outliers, and any potential problems with the data.
\item
  Visualization of categorical data: Seaborn offers many types of
  categorical charts, such as bar plots, box plots, violin plots, and
  point plots. Thanks to this, it is easy to compare values between
  different categories, which helps to better understand the data.
\item
  Visualization of multidimensional data: Seaborn allows you to create
  charts with many variables at once. Functions such as
  \texttt{pairplot} and \texttt{heatmap} are useful for analyzing
  multidimensional data and identifying correlations between variables.
\item
  Visualization of statistical distributions: Seaborn enables the
  creation of histograms, kernel density estimation (KDE) plots, and the
  empirical cumulative distribution function. With these tools, you can
  understand the distribution of data, which is essential in statistical
  analysis and modeling.
\item
  Regression visualization: Seaborn offers tools for regression
  analysis, such as \texttt{regplot} and \texttt{lmplot}. These
  functions allow for the visualization of the regression line, which
  makes it easier to understand the relationship between variables and
  to assess the fit of models.
\item
  Creating grids of charts: Seaborn allows you to create grids of charts
  using functions such as \texttt{FacetGrid} and \texttt{PairGrid}. This
  makes it easier to analyze and compare data for different subgroups,
  layers, or combinations of variables.
\item
  Customizing charts: Seaborn enables the customization of charts by
  changing styles, color palettes, and other chart parameters. Thanks to
  this, you can create attractive and professional-looking data
  visualizations.
\item
  Presentations and reports: Seaborn can be used to create high-quality
  data visualizations for the purposes of presentations, reports, or
  scientific publications. The aesthetics and ease of customization of
  charts make the visualizations created in Seaborn readable and
  engaging for the audience.
\item
  Time analysis: Seaborn can be used to analyze time data, such as time
  series or seasonal data. Functions such as \texttt{lineplot} or
  \texttt{relplot} allow for the visualization of trends and any changes
  in the data over time.
\item
  Comparison of models and algorithms: Data visualizations created using
  Seaborn can be used to compare the results of different machine
  learning models or algorithms. In this way, you can present the
  results of an analysis, the quality of classification, estimation, or
  forecasting.
\item
  Teaching and education: Seaborn is often used as a tool for teaching
  and education, especially in the context of learning statistics, data
  analysis, and machine learning. Data visualizations make it easier to
  understand complex concepts and relationships between variables.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Loading built-in datasets}\label{loading-built-in-datasets}

The \texttt{sns.load\_dataset()} function allows you to load built-in
datasets in the Seaborn library. All built-in datasets are stored as
Pandas DataFrames.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Loading the ``iris'' dataset:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}

\NormalTok{iris\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sns.load\_dataset(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}iris\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\BuiltInTok{print}\NormalTok{(iris\_data.head())}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
   sepal_length  sepal_width  petal_length  petal_width species

2           4.7          3.2           1.3          0.2  setosa
3           4.6          3.1           1.5          0.2  setosa
4           5.0          3.6           1.4          0.2  setosa
\end{verbatim}

\section{Scatter plot}\label{scatter-plot}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\CommentTok{\# Loading the data}
\NormalTok{iris\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sns.load\_dataset(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}iris\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Creating the scatter plot}
\NormalTok{sns.scatterplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_length\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_width\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{iris\_data)}

\CommentTok{\# Adding a title and axis labels}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Scatter plot of sepal length and width\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Sepal length (cm)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Sepal width (cm)\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Displaying the chart}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-5-output-1.pdf}}

The \texttt{sns.scatterplot()} function offers additional parameters
that allow for modifying the chart. Examples include:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{hue} parameter: allows you to add coloring of the points
  based on the values of a categorical variable.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\CommentTok{\# Loading the data}
\NormalTok{iris\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sns.load\_dataset(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}iris\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Creating a scatter plot with the \textquotesingle{}hue\textquotesingle{} parameter}

\section{Line plot}\label{line-plot}

The \texttt{sns.lineplot()} function in the Seaborn library is used to
create line plots, which allow for the visualization of the relationship
between two variables, especially in the case of time data. A line plot
is useful for presenting trends and changes in data over time or another
continuous variable.

Here is an example of using the \texttt{sns.lineplot()} function:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\CommentTok{\# Example data}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{2010}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2011}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2012}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2013}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2014}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2015}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2016}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2017}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2018}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2019}\NormalTok{],}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{110}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{105}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{130}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{140}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{150}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{170}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{200}\NormalTok{]}
\NormalTok{\}}

\CommentTok{\# Loading the data as a Pandas DataFrame}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\NormalTok{df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(data)}

\CommentTok{\# Creating the line plot}
\NormalTok{sns.lineplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df)}

\CommentTok{\# Adding a title and axis labels}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Line plot example\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Displaying the chart}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-9-output-1.pdf}}

In the example above, we create a line plot based on the DataFrame
\texttt{df}. The \texttt{x} and \texttt{y} parameters specify the
variables that are to be presented on the chart axes. The \texttt{data}
parameter indicates the data source, in this case a Pandas DataFrame.

The \texttt{sns.lineplot()} function offers additional parameters that
allow for modifying the chart. Examples include:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{hue} parameter: allows you to add coloring of the lines
  based on the values of a categorical variable.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}

\CommentTok{\# Example data}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{2010}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2011}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2012}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2013}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2014}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2015}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2016}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2017}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2018}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2019}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{,}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{110}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{105}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{130}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{140}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{150}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{170}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{200}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{+}
\NormalTok{             [}\DecValTok{200}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{170}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{150}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{140}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{130}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{120}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{110}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{100}\NormalTok{],}
    \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{10} \OperatorTok{+}\NormalTok{ [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{] }\OperatorTok{*} \DecValTok{10}
\NormalTok{\}}

\CommentTok{\# Loading the data as a Pandas DataFrame}
\NormalTok{df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(data)}

\CommentTok{\# Creating a line plot with the \textquotesingle{}hue\textquotesingle{} parameter}
\NormalTok{sns.lineplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, hue}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df)}

\CommentTok{\# Adding a title and axis labels}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Line plot example with the hue parameter\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.xlabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.ylabel(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Displaying the chart}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-10-output-1.pdf}}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{1}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{style} parameter: allows you to change the style of the
  line based on the values of a categorical variable.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.lineplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, style}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{2}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{markers} parameter: allows you to add markers to the data
  points.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.lineplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, markers}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{True}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{3}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{ci} parameter: allows you to add a confidence interval to
  the chart, which can be useful in the case of multiple measurements
  for the same values on the X axis.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.lineplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}year\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, ci}\OperatorTok{=}\DecValTok{95}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{Pie chart}\label{pie-chart}

Not directly supported.

\section{Bar chart}\label{bar-chart}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ pandas }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ pd}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\CommentTok{\# Example DataFrame}
\NormalTok{data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ \{}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}C\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}D\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}C\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}D\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{],}
        \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\DecValTok{10}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{15}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{8}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{11}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{14}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{9}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{13}\NormalTok{],}
        \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Group\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{: [}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}X\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}X\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}X\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}X\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Y\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Y\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Y\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Y\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]\}}
\NormalTok{df }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ pd.DataFrame(data)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Basic bar chart:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.barplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Basic bar chart\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-12-output-1.pdf}}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Example with \texttt{estimator}:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.barplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df, estimator}\OperatorTok{=}\BuiltInTok{max}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{"Bar chart with \textquotesingle{}estimator=max\textquotesingle{}"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-13-output-1.pdf}}

In this example, \texttt{estimator=max} causes the height of the bars to
be the maximum value for each category.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{1}
\tightlist
\item
  Example with \texttt{errorbar}:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.barplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df, errorbar}\OperatorTok{=}\VariableTok{None}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{"Bar chart with \textquotesingle{}errorbar=None\textquotesingle{}"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-14-output-1.pdf}}

Here, \texttt{errorbar=None} causes the confidence intervals not to be
displayed on the chart.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{2}
\tightlist
\item
  Example with \texttt{palette}:
\end{enumerate}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.barplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df, palette}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Greens\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, hue}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{"Bar chart with \textquotesingle{}palette=Greens\textquotesingle{}"}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-15-output-1.pdf}}

The \texttt{palette=\textquotesingle{}Greens\textquotesingle{}} argument
sets the color palette to shades of green.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{3}
\tightlist

  Example with \texttt{hue}:
\end{enumerate}

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-16-output-1.pdf}}

In this example, the
\texttt{hue=\textquotesingle{}Group\textquotesingle{}} argument splits
the bars for each category according to the values in the `Group'
column.

\begin{enumerate}

  Example with \texttt{orient}:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}

  Example with \texttt{order}:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{sns.barplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Category\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Value\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{df, order}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{[}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}D\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}C\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{])}
\NormalTok{plt.title(}\StringTok{"Bar chart with \textquotesingle{}order=[\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}D\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}C\textquotesingle{}]\textquotesingle{}"}\NormalTok{)}

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-18-output-1.pdf}}

The
\texttt{order={[}\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{},\ \textquotesingle{}D\textquotesingle{},\ \textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{},\ \textquotesingle{}C\textquotesingle{}{]}}
argument specifies the order of the categories on the x axis.

\section{Styles}\label{styles-1}

The Seaborn library allows you to customize the aesthetics of charts
using color palettes and styles, which lets you obtain attractive and
readable data visualizations. Here are a few examples of how we can
customize the aesthetics of charts in Seaborn:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Color palettes:
\end{enumerate}

Color palettes allow you to change the coloring of charts. Seaborn
offers several built-in color palettes that can be easily applied to
charts.

Example of using the `coolwarm' color palette in a scatter plot:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{iris\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sns.load\_dataset(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}iris\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Setting the \textquotesingle{}coolwarm\textquotesingle{} color palette}
\NormalTok{sns.set\_palette(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}coolwarm\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{sns.scatterplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_length\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_width\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, hue}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}species\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{iris\_data)}

\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-19-output-1.pdf}}

To reset the color palette to the default, use
\texttt{sns.set\_palette(\textquotesingle{}deep\textquotesingle{})}.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{1}
\tightlist
\item
  Chart styles:
\end{enumerate}

Seaborn allows you to change the style of charts, which can affect the
overall appearance and readability of the visualization. The library
offers several built-in styles.

Example of using the `whitegrid' style in a scatter plot:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{iris\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sns.load\_dataset(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}iris\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Setting the \textquotesingle{}whitegrid\textquotesingle{} style}
\NormalTok{sns.set\_style(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}whitegrid\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{sns.scatterplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_length\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_width\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, hue}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}species\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{iris\_data)}

\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-20-output-1.pdf}}

Other available styles are: `darkgrid', `white', `ticks', and `dark'. To
reset the style to the default, use
\texttt{sns.set\_style(\textquotesingle{}darkgrid\textquotesingle{})}.

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\setcounter{enumi}{2}
\tightlist
\item
  Scaling of graphical elements:
\end{enumerate}

Seaborn allows you to scale graphical elements, which can be useful in
the case of different screen resolutions or the need to change the size
of charts.

Example of using the `poster' context in a scatter plot:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ seaborn }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ sns}
\ImportTok{import}\NormalTok{ matplotlib.pyplot }\ImportTok{as}\NormalTok{ plt}

\NormalTok{iris\_data }\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{ sns.load\_dataset(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}iris\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# Setting the \textquotesingle{}poster\textquotesingle{} context}
\NormalTok{sns.set\_context(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}poster\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{sns.scatterplot(x}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_length\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, y}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}sepal\_width\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, hue}\OperatorTok{=}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}species\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, data}\OperatorTok{=}\NormalTok{iris\_data)}

\NormalTok{plt.show()}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\pandocbounded{\includegraphics[keepaspectratio]{seaborn-basics_files/figure-pdf/cell-21-output-1.pdf}}

Other available contexts are: `paper', `notebook', and `talk'. To reset
the context to the default, use
\texttt{sns.set\_context(\textquotesingle{}notebook\textquotesingle{})}.

By combining these methods, you can create varied, attractive, and
readable data visualizations.
